Purpose |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
This document provides crosswalk tables mapping all 398 ARA Autonomous Control Requirements (ACRs) to major regulatory and standards frameworks. It enables organizations pursuing ARA certification to understand evidence reuse opportunities, identify compliance gaps, and streamline multi-framework compliance programs. Each framework tab shows the specific mapping between ACRs and framework requirements, coverage statistics, and gap analysis. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Framework Coverage Summary |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Framework | Full Name / Edition | ACRs Mapped | % of Total ACRs | Unique Requirements Mapped | Tab Name |  |  |  |

 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
How to Use This Document |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
1. Start with this Overview tab to understand which frameworks have ARA mappings and coverage levels. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
2. Navigate to the framework-specific tab for your compliance program. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
3. Each framework tab shows: ACR ID, ARA domain, requirement statement, specific framework reference, evidence type, and evidence reuse guidance. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
4. Use the Master Crosswalk tab for a consolidated view of all ACR-to-framework mappings in a single matrix. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
5. Use the Gap Analysis tab to identify what each framework requires that ARA does not directly address. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
6. Filter columns in any tab to focus on specific domains, certification levels, or risk weights. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Gap Analysis — Framework Requirements Not Directly Covered by ARA |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Framework Requirement Area | Gap Description / Supplemental Action Required |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Govern 2.x — Organizational AI Governance Structures | ARA focuses on system-level controls, not organizational governance structures. Organizations should supplement ARA with internal governance policies. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Map 2.x — Broader Societal Impact Assessment | ARA evaluates operational reliability, not broader societal impact. Separate social impact assessments are recommended. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Map 3.x — AI Benefits Assessment | ARA does not assess benefits or positive impact — only operational reliability and safety. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Manage 3.x — Third-Party Risk Communication | ARA covers multi-party monitoring but not full third-party risk communication programs. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Manage 4.x — Organizational Change Management | ARA does not cover organizational change management processes related to AI deployment. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

=== SHEET: EU AI Act ===

ARA ↔ EU AI Act Mapping |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

ARAF-ARA-REG-2026-002  |  © 2026 Autonomous Reliability Assurance Foundation |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
The EU AI Act establishes a risk-based regulatory framework for AI systems in the European Union, with requirements scaling by risk classification from prohibited practices to minimal risk. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Coverage of ARA Standard | 16.8% |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Unique Framework References | 6 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Assurance Class — Ongoing Monitoring Framework |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
ARA Assurance Class (Class A Periodic / Class B Monitored / Class C Continuously Assured) maps to EU AI Act ongoing monitoring obligations for high-risk AI systems (Art. 9, Art. 72). Class C systems are required where the EU AI Act mandates continuous post-market surveillance. Class B satisfies periodic logging and review obligations. Class A is appropriate for minimal-risk or general-purpose AI with no ongoing monitoring mandate. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Gap Analysis — Framework Requirements Not Directly Covered by ARA |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Framework Requirement Area | Gap Description / Supplemental Action Required |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Art. 6–7 — Risk Classification System | ARA uses its own certification levels rather than EU risk classification. Organizations must independently determine their EU risk category. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Art. 10 — Training Data Governance | ARA evaluates system behavior, not training data practices. Organizations must separately address data governance requirements. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Art. 16–23 — Provider/Deployer Obligations | ARA certifies system capabilities, not organizational compliance roles (CE marking, registration, post-market monitoring responsibilities). |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Art. 26–27 — Fundamental Rights Impact Assessment | ARA does not include fundamental rights impact assessments. These must be conducted separately for EU compliance. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Art. 50 — General Transparency Obligations | ARA Domain 12 covers auditability but not all EU-specific transparency disclosure requirements for end users. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Art. 53–55 — General-Purpose AI Model Obligations | ARA evaluates deployed systems, not foundation models. GPAI-specific obligations (model cards, compute reporting) are out of scope. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

ISO/IEC 42001:2023 specifies requirements for establishing, implementing, maintaining, and continually improving an AI Management System (AIMS) within organizations. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Assurance Class — Ongoing Monitoring Framework |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
ARA Assurance Class (Class A Periodic / Class B Monitored / Class C Continuously Assured) operationalizes ISO/IEC 42001 continual improvement requirements (Clause 10) and performance evaluation obligations (Clause 9). Class C systems align with ISO 42001's highest monitoring intensity for AI systems with significant organizational or societal impact. Class B satisfies standard ISO 42001 monitoring and measurement requirements. Class A is appropriate for AI applications with limited operational risk where annual management review cycles are sufficient. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Gap Analysis — Framework Requirements Not Directly Covered by ARA |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Framework Requirement Area | Gap Description / Supplemental Action Required |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Clause 4 — Context of the Organization | ARA does not assess organizational context, stakeholder needs, or management system scope definition. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Clause 5 — Leadership and Commitment | ARA does not evaluate leadership engagement, AI policy establishment, or organizational roles/responsibilities. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Clause 7.1–7.4 — Resources, Competence, Awareness, Communication | ARA evaluates system capabilities, not organizational resource allocation, staff competency, or communication processes. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Clause 9.1 — Monitoring and Measurement of AIMS | ARA monitors system behavior, not AIMS management system effectiveness. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Clause 10 — Continual Improvement of AIMS | ARA addresses system drift and revalidation but not AIMS-level nonconformity management and continual improvement processes. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Gap Analysis — Framework Requirements Not Directly Covered by ARA |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Framework Requirement Area | Gap Description / Supplemental Action Required |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Clause 4–6 — ISMS Context, Leadership, Planning | ARA evaluates technical controls, not ISMS management system establishment and governance. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
A.5.1–A.5.4 — Information Security Policies | ARA does not assess organizational security policy documentation or management direction. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
A.6.1–A.6.8 — People Controls (Screening, Terms, Awareness, Training) | ARA does not cover human resources security — screening, terms of employment, security training. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
A.7 — Physical Security Controls | ARA Domain 15 covers physical actuation but not facility physical security (perimeters, offices, equipment). |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
A.5.19–A.5.23 — Supplier Relationship Security | ARA covers multi-party monitoring but not full supply chain information security management. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Gap Analysis — Framework Requirements Not Directly Covered by ARA |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Framework Requirement Area | Gap Description / Supplemental Action Required |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
CP — Contingency Planning (CP-1 through CP-13) | ARA covers failure modes and recovery but not full organizational contingency planning, backup, and disaster recovery programs. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
MA — Maintenance (MA-1 through MA-7) | ARA does not address system maintenance scheduling, controlled maintenance, or maintenance tools/personnel. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
MP — Media Protection (MP-1 through MP-8) | ARA does not cover media access, marking, storage, transport, sanitization, or disposal. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
PE — Physical and Environmental Protection | ARA Domain 15 covers physical actuation safety, not facility physical access, environmental controls, or power/cabling protection. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
PS — Personnel Security (PS-1 through PS-9) | ARA does not cover personnel screening, termination, transfer, or access agreement requirements. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
PT — PII Processing and Transparency | ARA does not address privacy-specific controls for personally identifiable information processing. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Gap Analysis — Framework Requirements Not Directly Covered by ARA |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Framework Requirement Area | Gap Description / Supplemental Action Required |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
CC1 — Control Environment | ARA does not assess organizational control environment (management philosophy, integrity, ethical values, HR policies). |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
CC2 — Communication and Information | ARA covers system monitoring and telemetry but not organizational information and communication processes. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
CC3 — Risk Assessment | ARA defines risk weights per ACR but does not substitute for organizational risk assessment processes. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
A1.2 — Environmental Protections and Recovery | ARA covers system-level failures but not infrastructure availability, environmental protections, or disaster recovery testing. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
P1 — Privacy Criteria | ARA does not cover privacy notice, choice/consent, collection, use/retention/disposal, access, disclosure, or quality of personal information. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Gap Analysis — Framework Requirements Not Directly Covered by ARA |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Framework Requirement Area | Gap Description / Supplemental Action Required |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Part 2 — Hardware Safety Integrity | ARA focuses on software and decision-layer safety. Hardware failure rates, diagnostic coverage, and hardware fault tolerance are not directly assessed. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Part 3, Clause 7.4 — Software Architecture Design | ARA evaluates behavioral reliability, not internal software architecture design and coding standards. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
SIL Determination — Risk Graph / LOPA Methods | ARA does not include SIL determination methodology. Organizations must independently determine applicable SIL targets. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Part 1, Clause 7.6 — Installation and Commissioning | ARA does not cover physical installation, commissioning, or site acceptance testing procedures. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Part 1, Clause 7.8 — Modification and Retrofit | ARA covers drift detection and revalidation but not formal SIL recalculation for system modifications. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Gap Analysis — Framework Requirements Not Directly Covered by ARA |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Framework Requirement Area | Gap Description / Supplemental Action Required |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Part 2-1 — IACS Security Management System | ARA does not replace the need for a full IACS security management system including policies, organization, and risk assessment. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Part 2-4 — Security Program Requirements for IACS Service Providers | ARA certifies systems, not service provider security programs. Service providers must separately comply. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Part 3-2 — Security Risk Assessment for System Design | ARA does not perform zone/conduit analysis or threat modeling specific to industrial network architecture. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Part 4-1 — Secure Product Development Lifecycle | ARA evaluates deployed behavior, not product development lifecycle security requirements. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Security Levels (SL 1–4) | ARA certification levels are not equivalent to IEC 62443 Security Levels. Separate SL determination is required. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Gap Analysis — Framework Requirements Not Directly Covered by ARA |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Framework Requirement Area | Gap Description / Supplemental Action Required |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
LLM-04 — Model Denial of Service | ARA Domain 7 covers behavioral reliability under stress but does not specifically address model-level denial of service attack vectors and resource exhaustion. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
LLM-05 — Supply Chain Vulnerabilities | ARA does not cover LLM supply chain risks including compromised model weights, poisoned training data from third parties, or malicious plugins in the supply chain. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
LLM-08 — Excessive Agency | ARA Domain 1 (Autonomy Scope) addresses boundary definition but OWASP LLM-08 also covers excessive functionality, permissions, and autonomy in specific LLM integration contexts. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
LLM-09 — Overreliance | ARA covers human override (Domain 10) but does not specifically address user overreliance on LLM outputs or the need for output validation workflows. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
LLM-10 — Model Theft | ARA does not directly address model theft, model extraction attacks, or intellectual property protection of the underlying model. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

=== SHEET: ISO 42005 ===

ARA ↔ ISO/IEC 42005:2025 Mapping |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ARAF-ARA-REG-2026-002  |  © 2026 Autonomous Reliability Assurance Foundation |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 42005:2025 (AI System Impact Assessment) provides guidance for conducting structured impact assessments throughout the AI system lifecycle. Clause 5 defines the 10-step assessment process (scope, responsibilities, thresholds, performance, analysis, recording, approval, monitoring). Clause 6 defines documentation requirements (AI system info, data quality, algorithm info, deployment environment, stakeholders, actual and foreseeable impacts, mitigation). This crosswalk maps ARA ACRs to ISO 42005 clauses, enabling evidence reuse for EU AI Act high-risk system impact assessment obligations. |  |  |  |  |  |  |

=== SHEET: ISO 42006 ===

ARA ↔ ISO/IEC 42006:2025 Mapping |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ARAF-ARA-REG-2026-002  |  © 2026 Autonomous Reliability Assurance Foundation |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 42006:2025 specifies requirements for bodies providing audit and certification of AI Management Systems (AIMS) per ISO/IEC 42001. Published July 2025, it governs certification body competence, impartiality, audit processes, decision-making, and maintaining certification. It directly informs ARA Authorized Validation Body (AVB) accreditation requirements. ARA ACRs in Domains 9, 12, and 14 are the primary areas of alignment, covering operational governance, auditability, and performance monitoring — the system-side evidence that AVBs must assess. |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Coverage of ARA Standard | 10.1% |  |  |  |  |  | 
Unique Framework References | 14 |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |

ACR-14.21 | Domain 14: Operational Governance Controls | Compliance status SHALL be tracked and reported to designated governance stakeholders at defined intervals. | ISO 42006 Cl.5.1 | EI | Governance documentation; change control records. | Compliance reporting records; stakeholder distribution evidence. | ARA governance evidence satisfies ISO 42006 structural and management system requirements for certification body oversight.
ACR-14.22 | Domain 14: Operational Governance Controls | Governance documentation SHALL be reviewed and approved by designated authorities before publication. | ISO 42006 Cl.5.1 | EI | Governance documentation; change control records. | Document approval records; authority designation documentation. | ARA governance evidence satisfies ISO 42006 structural and management system requirements for certification body oversight.
ACR-14.23 | Domain 14: Operational Governance Controls | Where a Deployment Certification claims Certification Inheritance from a Platform-Certified product, the deploying organization SHALL document the configuration match between the deployment and the Platform Cert reference environment. The AVB SHALL verify this match and attest to it in the Deployment Cert evaluation report. | ISO 42006 Cl.5.1 | EI | Governance documentation; change control records. | Configuration match documentation; AVB attestation in Deployment Cert evaluation report. | ARA governance evidence satisfies ISO 42006 structural and management system requirements for certification body oversight.
ACR-14.24 | Domain 14: Operational Governance Controls | The deploying organization SHALL notify the platform vendor and ARAF within 14 days of any deployment-side configuration change that affects inherited ACR coverage. Changes that invalidate inherited coverage SHALL trigger a delta evaluation of affected ACRs. | ISO 42006 Cl.5.1 | EI | Governance documentation; change control records. | Configuration change notification records; delta evaluation documentation. | ARA governance evidence satisfies ISO 42006 structural and management system requirements for certification body oversight.
ACR-14.25 | Domain 14: Operational Governance Controls | If the deploying organization materially changes the system's operational context in a manner that would increase the Risk Classification (e.g., expanding from internal to customer-facing deployment, adding life-safety use cases, or entering a regulated domain), the organization SHALL notify ARAF and the evaluating AVB within 14 days. The AVB SHALL conduct a Risk Classification reassessment to determine whether the Assurance Class must be elevated. | ISO 42006 Cl.5.1 | EI | Governance documentation; change control records. | Operational context change notification records; Risk Classification reassessment documentation. | ARA governance evidence satisfies ISO 42006 structural and management system requirements for certification body oversight.

=== SHEET: AAIF MCP ===

ARA ↔ AAIF / Model Context Protocol — Complementary Layer Reference |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ARAF-ARA-REG-2026-002  |  © 2026 Autonomous Reliability Assurance Foundation |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
The Agentic AI Foundation (AAIF), a Linux Foundation initiative founded December 2025, provides neutral governance for open agentic AI interoperability standards: Anthropic's Model Context Protocol (MCP), OpenAI's AGENTS.md, and Block's Goose framework. Founding members include AWS, Google, Microsoft, Bloomberg, and Cloudflare. AAIF governs the connectivity and interoperability layer; ARA governs behavioral reliability and safety assurance. These are complementary, non-competing layers. AAIF compliance does not substitute for ARA certification, and ARA certification does not replace AAIF interoperability standards. Note: AAIF has no numbered control requirements. This sheet uses a complementary-layer reference structure rather than a traditional ACR crosswalk. |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
⚠  COMPLEMENTARY LAYER REFERENCE: AAIF/MCP is an interoperability protocol, not a numbered control framework. No ACR-to-clause mapping is applicable. This sheet documents the architectural relationship between AAIF components and ARA domains. |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Layer Architecture Overview |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Layer | Function | Scope | ARA Relationship |  |  |  | 
AAIF / MCP | Connectivity & Interoperability | How agents connect to tools, data, services, and each other | Defines the protocol stack within which ARA-certified systems operate |  |  |  | 
AAIF / AGENTS.md | Behavioral Conventions | Project-specific guidance files for coding agent behavior | Provides context artifacts relevant to D1, D2, D14 ARA evaluations |  |  |  | 
AAIF / Goose | Reference Implementation | Open-source local-first agent framework using MCP | Reference implementation that ARA certification scope can include |  |  |  | 
ARA Standard | Reliability & Safety Assurance | Behavioral, operational, and safety requirements for autonomous systems | Provides verifiable conformity assessment layer above AAIF protocols |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
ARA Domain ↔ AAIF Component Relationship |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
ARA Domain | Domain ACRs | AAIF Component | Protocol / Spec | Relationship Type | ARA Scope Note | AAIF Scope Note | Evidence Relevance
Domain 2: Decision Integrity | 32 | AGENTS.md | OpenAI AGENTS.md v1 (AAIF-governed) | Contextual Reference | ACRs govern verifiable behavioral compliance of agent decisions | AGENTS.md provides behavioral conventions that evaluators may reference as context artifacts | AGENTS.md files are relevant evidence artifacts during D2 evaluation; not a substitute for ARA conformity assessment
Domain 3: Tool and API Governance | 28 | MCP (Model Context Protocol) | MCP Specification v1.x (AAIF-governed) | Complementary | ACRs govern integrity, authorization, and safety of tool/API interactions | MCP defines how agents connect to tools and APIs; ARA governs whether those connections behave safely | MCP server inventory and tool manifests may serve as evidence artifacts for D3 tool registry ACRs
Domain 4: Identity and Permission Containment | 22 | MCP (Authorization) | MCP Auth / OAuth 2.0 (AAIF-governed) | Complementary | ACRs govern identity verification and permission enforcement at runtime | MCP defines OAuth-based authorization for agent-tool sessions; ARA verifies authorization controls work correctly | MCP OAuth configuration records are relevant evidence for D4 authorization ACRs
Domain 8: Adversarial Robustness | 38 | MCP (Security Surface) | MCP Specification + CoSAI MCP Security (Jan 2026) | Complementary | ACRs govern adversarial resilience of MCP-connected systems | AAIF defines the connectivity protocol whose security posture ARA evaluates; CoSAI MCP Security taxonomy informs threat scenarios | MCP connection security posture is directly within D8 evaluation scope for ARA-certified agentic systems
Domain 14: Operational Governance Controls | 25 | AAIF Governance Model | Linux Foundation AAIF Charter (Dec 2025) | Reference | ACRs govern organizational operational governance of certified systems | AAIF governance model is a reference for multi-agent system operational governance structure | AAIF membership and governance compliance may serve as supporting context for D14 organizational governance ACRs
 |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Applicable to all ARA-certified systems that use MCP as their tool integration protocol. AAIF compliance is assumed as a precondition for MCP-connected systems; it does not reduce ARA evaluation scope. |  |  |  |  |  |  | 

=== SHEET: NIST AI Agent ===

ARA ↔ NIST AI Agent Standards Initiative — Forward-Looking Reference |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ARAF-ARA-REG-2026-002  |  © 2026 Autonomous Reliability Assurance Foundation |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
NIST's Center for AI Standards and Innovation (CAISI) announced the AI Agent Standards Initiative in February 2026. The initiative's three pillars are: (1) facilitating industry-led standards and U.S. leadership in international bodies, (2) fostering community-led open-source protocol development, and (3) advancing research on AI agent security and identity. CAISI issued an RFI on AI Agent Security (responses due March 9, 2026) and a draft Concept Paper on AI Agent Identity and Authorization (due April 2, 2026). Sector-specific listening sessions are planned for April 2026. No published control framework exists as of March 2026; anticipated deliverables are expected H2 2026. |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
⚠  FORWARD-LOOKING REFERENCE — NO PUBLISHED CONTROLS AS OF MARCH 2026: The NIST AI Agent Standards Initiative was announced February 2026. No control framework, guidelines, or numbered requirements have been published. This sheet documents ARA's anticipated alignment based on NIST's stated focus pillars. This sheet will be fully updated upon NIST publication of agent-specific guidelines (expected H2 2026). Organizations should not cite this sheet for current compliance purposes. |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Initiative Status and Timeline |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Milestone | Status | Date / Deadline | ARA Relevance |  |  |  | 
AI Agent Standards Initiative Launch | Complete | February 2026 | Signals federal commitment to agent-specific standards; ARA positioned as conformity assessment layer |  |  |  | 
RFI on AI Agent Security | Open | March 9, 2026 (deadline) | ARAF should provide input; RFI responses will shape security control priorities |  |  |  | 
Draft Concept Paper: Agent Identity and Authorization | Open for comment | April 2, 2026 (deadline) | Directly relevant to ARA Domain 4 (Identity/Permission) and Domain 2 (Decision Integrity) |  |  |  | 
Sector Listening Sessions (Finance, Healthcare, Education) | Planned | April 2026 | Sector deployment guidance will inform ARA industry-specific evaluation supplements |  |  |  | 
NIST AI Agent Guidelines Publication | Anticipated | H2 2026 (estimated) | Upon publication, this sheet will be converted to a full ACR-level crosswalk |  |  |  | 
International Standards Alignment | Ongoing | 2026–2027 | NIST participation in ISO/IEC JTC 1/SC 42 work will influence ISO 42001/42005 updates relevant to ARA |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
NIST Initiative Pillars ↔ ARA Domain Alignment (Anticipated) |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
NIST Pillar / Focus Area | Anticipated Scope | Primary ARA Domain(s) | Domain ACRs | Anticipated Alignment Basis | Current ARA Coverage | Gap Notes | 
Security Controls and Risk Management | Safeguards and risk management frameworks tailored to AI agents; controls for misuse, compromise, privilege escalation, unintended autonomous actions | D6: Failure Mode Containment
D8: Adversarial Robustness | 28 + 38 = 66 | ARA D6 and D8 directly address agent-specific failure modes and adversarial risks | Strong — ARA already covers threat mitigations NIST is targeting | May need agent-specific attestation formats once NIST publishes | 
Threat Models and Attack Surfaces | Identification of vulnerabilities unique to AI agents: autonomous task execution, tool use, API integrations, cross-system access | D8: Adversarial Robustness
D3: Tool and API Governance | 38 + 28 = 66 | ARA D8 adversarial robustness and D3 tool governance directly address agent attack surfaces | Strong — ARA ACRs cover prompt injection, tool poisoning, API boundary failures | NIST may define agent-specific threat taxonomy requiring new ARA test scenarios | 
Governance and Oversight Controls | Human supervision, escalation protocols, access controls, accountability for agent behavior in production | D11: Escalation and Human Override
D14: Operational Governance Controls
D4: Identity and Permission Containment | 22 + 25 + 22 = 69 | ARA D11 (human override), D14 (operational governance), and D4 (identity/permissions) collectively address NIST oversight priorities | Strong — core ARA coverage; agent-specific override requirements already addressed | Accountability structures for multi-agent systems may require ARA D14 expansion | 
Secure Development Lifecycle Practices | Controls for designing, testing, deploying AI agents: validation, red-teaming, change management | D12: Auditability and Transparency
D14: Operational Governance Controls | 26 + 25 = 51 | ARA D12 (auditability) and D14 (change control, release governance) address SDLC practices | Moderate — ARA covers post-deployment; NIST may require pre-deployment agent validation evidence | May require ARA evaluation methodology supplement for pre-deployment agent testing | 
Monitoring, Logging and Incident Response | Auditing agent activity, traceability of actions, responding to security incidents and unintended outcomes | D10: Monitoring and Telemetry
D12: Auditability and Transparency | 30 + 26 = 56 | ARA D10 (telemetry) and D12 (audit trails) directly address agent activity monitoring and traceability | Strong — ARA telemetry and audit requirements are agent-appropriate | Incident response specifics for multi-agent chains may need ARA evaluation guidance | 
AI Agent Identity and Authorization | Standards for identifying, managing, and authorizing access and actions taken by software agents | D4: Identity and Permission Containment
D2: Decision Integrity | 22 + 32 = 54 | ARA D4 directly governs agent identity verification and permission containment; D2 governs authorized decision execution | Strong — ARA D4 covers non-human identity lifecycle, token management, and privilege controls | NIST Concept Paper (NCCoE) on identity standards for agents may drive ARA D4 updates | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Anticipated ACR Coverage Upon NIST Publication |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
Based on NIST's stated focus pillars, ARA anticipates mapping 150–200 ACRs across D2, D3, D4, D6, D8, D10, D11, D12, and D14 upon NIST publication of agent-specific guidelines. This would represent approximately 38–50% ARA standard coverage, comparable to NIST AI RMF mapping (48%). This sheet will be converted to a full ACR-level crosswalk format matching other regulatory sheets upon NIST guideline release. |  |  |  |  |  |  | 

=== SHEET: CoSAI ===

ARA ↔ CoSAI MCP Security Framework Mapping |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ARAF-ARA-REG-2026-002  |  © 2026 Autonomous Reliability Assurance Foundation |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
CoSAI (Coalition for Secure AI) is an OASIS Open Project founded July 2024, backed by Anthropic, Google, IBM, Microsoft, NVIDIA, PayPal, and 40+ partners. CoSAI published the MCP Security White Paper (January 8/27, 2026), establishing 12 threat categories and ~40 distinct threats for MCP-based AI agent deployments. CoSAI addresses AI security practices; ARA addresses reliability and behavioral assurance. This crosswalk maps CoSAI's 12 threat categories to the ARA ACRs that mitigate each threat class, enabling evidence reuse and threat-informed evaluation planning. |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Organizations may use ARA evaluation evidence to demonstrate CoSAI threat mitigations. |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
CoSAI Threat Category Summary (T1–T12) |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
CoSAI Ref | Threat Category | Description | Primary ARA Domains | ACRs Addressing Threat |  |  | 
T1 | Improper Authentication | Weak identity verification and credential management across agent chains | D4: Identity and Permission Containment | ACR-4.01 to ACR-4.12 |  |  | 
T2 | Missing Access Control | Insufficient authorization checks and privilege separation | D4: Identity and Permission Containment | ACR-4.13 to ACR-4.22 |  |  | 
T3 | Input Validation Failures | Traditional injection flaws amplified by AI-mediated tool execution | D3: Tool and API Governance, D8: Adversarial Robustness | ACR-3.01 to ACR-3.10, ACR-8.01 to ACR-8.08 |  |  | 
T4 | Data/Control Boundary Failures | Prompt injection and tool poisoning — LLM cannot distinguish instructions from data | D8: Adversarial Robustness, D2: Decision Integrity | ACR-8.09 to ACR-8.22, ACR-2.01 to ACR-2.08 |  |  | 
T5 | Inadequate Data Protection | Insufficient encryption and secrets management for agent-handled data | D5: Data Privacy and Information Protection | ACR-5.01 to ACR-5.12 |  |  |

T8 | Network Isolation Failures | Improper network binding and segmentation for MCP servers | D6: Failure Mode Containment, D4: Identity and Permission Containment | ACR-6.15 to ACR-6.22, ACR-4.01 to ACR-4.06 |  |  | 
T9 | Trust Boundary Failures | Overreliance on LLM judgment for security-critical decisions | D2: Decision Integrity, D8: Adversarial Robustness | ACR-2.01 to ACR-2.12, ACR-8.01 to ACR-8.12 |  |  | 
T10 | Resource Management Failures | Absence of rate limiting and quota controls enabling denial-of-service | D7: Behavioral Reliability Under Stress, D6: Failure Mode Containment | ACR-7.01 to ACR-7.10, ACR-6.01 to ACR-6.08 |  |  | 
T11 | Supply Chain Failures | Insecure MCP server lifecycle and distribution (rug pull, shadowing, typosquatting) | D3: Tool and API Governance, D14: Operational Governance Controls | ACR-3.01 to ACR-3.10, ACR-14.01 to ACR-14.08 |  |  | 
T12 | Insufficient Observability | Lack of logging, monitoring, and audit trails for agent actions | D10: Monitoring and Telemetry, D12: Auditability and Transparency | ACR-10.01 to ACR-10.12, ACR-12.01 to ACR-12.08 |  |  |

NIST AI RMF | Govern 2.x — Organizational AI Governance Structures | ARA focuses on system-level controls, not organizational governance structures. Organizations should supplement ARA with internal governance policies. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST AI RMF | Map 2.x — Broader Societal Impact Assessment | ARA evaluates operational reliability, not broader societal impact. Separate social impact assessments are recommended. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST AI RMF | Map 3.x — AI Benefits Assessment | ARA does not assess benefits or positive impact — only operational reliability and safety. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST AI RMF | Manage 3.x — Third-Party Risk Communication | ARA covers multi-party monitoring but not full third-party risk communication programs. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST AI RMF | Manage 4.x — Organizational Change Management | ARA does not cover organizational change management processes related to AI deployment. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
EU AI Act | Art. 6–7 — Risk Classification System | ARA uses its own certification levels rather than EU risk classification. Organizations must independently determine their EU risk category. | High | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
EU AI Act | Art. 10 — Training Data Governance | ARA evaluates system behavior, not training data practices. Organizations must separately address data governance requirements. | High | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
EU AI Act | Art. 16–23 — Provider/Deployer Obligations | ARA certifies system capabilities, not organizational compliance roles (CE marking, registration, post-market monitoring responsibilities). | High | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
EU AI Act | Art. 26–27 — Fundamental Rights Impact Assessment | ARA does not include fundamental rights impact assessments. These must be conducted separately for EU compliance. | High | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
EU AI Act | Art. 50 — General Transparency Obligations | ARA Domain 12 covers auditability but not all EU-specific transparency disclosure requirements for end users. | High | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
EU AI Act | Art. 53–55 — General-Purpose AI Model Obligations | ARA evaluates deployed systems, not foundation models. GPAI-specific obligations (model cards, compute reporting) are out of scope. | High | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 42001 | Clause 4 — Context of the Organization | ARA does not assess organizational context, stakeholder needs, or management system scope definition. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 42001 | Clause 5 — Leadership and Commitment | ARA does not evaluate leadership engagement, AI policy establishment, or organizational roles/responsibilities. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 42001 | Clause 7.1–7.4 — Resources, Competence, Awareness, Communication | ARA evaluates system capabilities, not organizational resource allocation, staff competency, or communication processes. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 42001 | Clause 9.1 — Monitoring and Measurement of AIMS | ARA monitors system behavior, not AIMS management system effectiveness. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 42001 | Clause 10 — Continual Improvement of AIMS | ARA addresses system drift and revalidation but not AIMS-level nonconformity management and continual improvement processes. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 27001 | Clause 4–6 — ISMS Context, Leadership, Planning | ARA evaluates technical controls, not ISMS management system establishment and governance. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 27001 | A.5.1–A.5.4 — Information Security Policies | ARA does not assess organizational security policy documentation or management direction. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 27001 | A.6.1–A.6.8 — People Controls (Screening, Terms, Awareness, Training) | ARA does not cover human resources security — screening, terms of employment, security training. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 27001 | A.7 — Physical Security Controls | ARA Domain 15 covers physical actuation but not facility physical security (perimeters, offices, equipment). | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
ISO/IEC 27001 | A.5.19–A.5.23 — Supplier Relationship Security | ARA covers multi-party monitoring but not full supply chain information security management. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST SP 800-53 | CP — Contingency Planning (CP-1 through CP-13) | ARA covers failure modes and recovery but not full organizational contingency planning, backup, and disaster recovery programs. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST SP 800-53 | MA — Maintenance (MA-1 through MA-7) | ARA does not address system maintenance scheduling, controlled maintenance, or maintenance tools/personnel. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST SP 800-53 | MP — Media Protection (MP-1 through MP-8) | ARA does not cover media access, marking, storage, transport, sanitization, or disposal. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST SP 800-53 | PE — Physical and Environmental Protection | ARA Domain 15 covers physical actuation safety, not facility physical access, environmental controls, or power/cabling protection. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST SP 800-53 | PS — Personnel Security (PS-1 through PS-9) | ARA does not cover personnel screening, termination, transfer, or access agreement requirements. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST SP 800-53 | PT — PII Processing and Transparency | ARA does not address privacy-specific controls for personally identifiable information processing. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
SOC 2 | CC1 — Control Environment | ARA does not assess organizational control environment (management philosophy, integrity, ethical values, HR policies). | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
SOC 2 | CC2 — Communication and Information | ARA covers system monitoring and telemetry but not organizational information and communication processes. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
SOC 2 | CC3 — Risk Assessment | ARA defines risk weights per ACR but does not substitute for organizational risk assessment processes. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
SOC 2 | A1.2 — Environmental Protections and Recovery | ARA covers system-level failures but not infrastructure availability, environmental protections, or disaster recovery testing. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
SOC 2 | P1 — Privacy Criteria | ARA does not cover privacy notice, choice/consent, collection, use/retention/disposal, access, disclosure, or quality of personal information. | Medium | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
IEC 61508 | Part 2 — Hardware Safety Integrity | ARA focuses on software and decision-layer safety. Hardware failure rates, diagnostic coverage, and hardware fault tolerance are not directly assessed. | High | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
IEC 61508 | Part 3, Clause 7.4 — Software Architecture Design | ARA evaluates behavioral reliability, not internal software architecture design and coding standards. | High | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
IEC 61508 | SIL Determination — Risk Graph / LOPA Methods | ARA does not include SIL determination methodology. Organizations must independently determine applicable SIL targets. | High | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
IEC 61508 | Part 1, Clause 7.6 — Installation and Commissioning | ARA does not cover physical installation, commissioning, or site acceptance testing procedures. | High | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
IEC 61508 | Part 1, Clause 7.8 — Modification and Retrofit | ARA covers drift detection and revalidation but not formal SIL recalculation for system modifications. | High | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
IEC 62443 | Part 2-1 — IACS Security Management System | ARA does not replace the need for a full IACS security management system including policies, organization, and risk assessment. | Low | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
IEC 62443 | Part 2-4 — Security Program Requirements for IACS Service Providers | ARA certifies systems, not service provider security programs. Service providers must separately comply. | Low | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
IEC 62443 | Part 3-2 — Security Risk Assessment for System Design | ARA does not perform zone/conduit analysis or threat modeling specific to industrial network architecture. | Low | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
IEC 62443 | Part 4-1 — Secure Product Development Lifecycle | ARA evaluates deployed behavior, not product development lifecycle security requirements. | Low | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
IEC 62443 | Security Levels (SL 1–4) | ARA certification levels are not equivalent to IEC 62443 Security Levels. Separate SL determination is required. | Low | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
OWASP LLM Top 10 | LLM-04 — Model Denial of Service | ARA Domain 7 covers behavioral reliability under stress but does not specifically address model-level denial of service attack vectors and resource exhaustion. | Low | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
OWASP LLM Top 10 | LLM-05 — Supply Chain Vulnerabilities | ARA does not cover LLM supply chain risks including compromised model weights, poisoned training data from third parties, or malicious plugins in the supply chain. | Low | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
OWASP LLM Top 10 | LLM-08 — Excessive Agency | ARA Domain 1 (Autonomy Scope) addresses boundary definition but OWASP LLM-08 also covers excessive functionality, permissions, and autonomy in specific LLM integration contexts. | Low | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
OWASP LLM Top 10 | LLM-09 — Overreliance | ARA covers human override (Domain 10) but does not specifically address user overreliance on LLM outputs or the need for output validation workflows. | Low | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
OWASP LLM Top 10 | LLM-10 — Model Theft | ARA does not directly address model theft, model extraction attacks, or intellectual property protection of the underlying model. | Low | Implement supplemental controls or document existing organizational policies that address this requirement. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST AI RMF | Map 2.x — Broader Societal Impact Assessment | Domain 13 (Societal Impact) now directly addresses societal impact assessment, substantially closing this gap. Residual: ARA does not assess positive societal benefits. | Low | Document residual gap; Domain 13 evidence covers most requirements. |  |  |  |  | 
NIST SP 800-53 | PT — PII Processing and Transparency | Domain 5 (Data Privacy) now directly addresses PII processing, data subject rights, and transparency. Residual: some PT controls address organizational privacy programs beyond system-level. | Low | Domain 5 evidence covers most PT requirements; supplement with organizational privacy documentation. |  |  |  |  | 
SOC 2 | P1 — Privacy Criteria | Domain 5 (Data Privacy) now addresses privacy notice, choice/consent, collection, and retention at the system level. Residual: organizational privacy governance. | Low | Domain 5 evidence covers system-level privacy; supplement with organizational privacy program documentation. |  |  |  |  | 
MITRE ATLAS | ML Supply Chain Compromise (AML.T0010) | ARA Domain 8 adversarial robustness covers supply chain integrity for ML models. Residual: organizational supply chain management beyond model artifacts. | Low | Implement supplemental organizational supply chain controls. |  |  |  |  | 
CSA AICM | AICM-GV-03 — AI Ethics Governance | ARA Domain 13 covers societal impact and responsible deployment. Residual: formal AI ethics committee establishment and review processes. | Low | Implement supplemental AI ethics governance controls. |  |  |  |  | 

=== SHEET: Evidence Reuse Guide ===

Evidence Reuse Guide |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ARAF-ARA-REG-2026-002  |  © 2026 Autonomous Reliability Assurance Foundation |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
This tab provides guidance on how ARA certification evidence can be reused across multiple compliance frameworks, reducing duplication of effort for organizations maintaining multi-framework compliance programs. |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | 
ARA Evidence Type | Description | NIST AI RMF | EU AI Act | ISO 42001 / 27001 | NIST 800-53 | SOC 2 | OWASP LLM | MITRE ATLAS | CSA AICM
Automated Test Reports | Results from automated ACR testing including pass/fail, test coverage, and regression analysis | ✓ Measure function | ✓ Art. 9, 15 | ✓ A.8.4, A.8.28 | ✓ CA-2, CA-7 | ✓ CC4.1, CC7.1 | ✓ All LLM categories | ✓ Adversarial technique testing | ✓ SE, RL categories
Human Simulation Results | Records from human-administered behavioral tests, including adversarial scenarios | ✓ Measure function | ✓ Art. 9 | ✓ A.8.4 | ✓ CA-2, CA-8 | ✓ CC4.1 | ✓ LLM-01, 02, 06 | ✓ Red team exercises | ✓ SF categories
Expert Inspection Reports | Formal reviews by qualified assessors of system design, configuration, and documentation | ✓ Govern, Map | ✓ Art. 9, 11 | ✓ A.6.1, A.7.5 | ✓ CA-2, RA-5 | ✓ CC3.2 | ✓ All categories | ✓ Threat model review | ✓ GV, TR categories
Continuous Monitoring Data | Ongoing telemetry from the accredited CAPO's CAP showing behavioral compliance over time | ✓ Manage function | ✓ Art. 9, 12 | ✓ A.8.4 | ✓ CA-7, SI-4 | ✓ CC7.1, CC7.2 | ✓ All categories | ✓ Adversarial monitoring | ✓ MO categories
Adversarial Test Batteries | Results from red team exercises and adversarial robustness testing | ✓ Measure, Manage | ✓ Art. 9 | ✓ A.8.4 | ✓ CA-8, RA-5 | ✓ CC4.1 | ✓ LLM-01, 02, 03 | ✓ All ATLAS techniques | ✓ SE categories
Boundary Specification Docs | Formal documentation of system autonomy boundaries, permitted/restricted actions | ✓ Map function | ✓ Art. 9, 13 | ✓ A.6.1, A.6.2 | ✓ AC-3, CM-7 | ✓ CC6.1 | ✓ LLM-07, 08 | ✓ Attack surface mapping | ✓ GV, AS categories
Decision Audit Trails | Complete records of autonomous decision chains with justification and provenance | ✓ Govern, Map | ✓ Art. 12, 13 | ✓ A.8.4 | ✓ AU-2, AU-3 | ✓ CC7.2, CC7.3 | ✓ LLM-06 | ✓ Decision manipulation | ✓ TR, AU categories
Drift Detection Reports | Analysis of behavioral drift over time with stability metrics and threshold alerts | ✓ Manage function | ✓ Art. 9, 15 | ✓ A.8.4 | ✓ SI-4, SI-7 | ✓ CC7.1 | ✓ LLM-09 | ✓ Model drift detection | ✓ MO categories
Escalation Protocol Records | Documentation of human override events, escalation triggers, and resolution outcomes | ✓ Govern, Manage | ✓ Art. 14 | ✓ A.6.1 | ✓ IR-1, IR-4 | ✓ CC7.3, CC7.4 | ✓ LLM-08 | ✓ Incident response | ✓ HO categories
Certification Reports | Formal ARA certification reports including domain scores, pass/fail, and conditions | ✓ All functions | ✓ Art. 11, 43 | ✓ Clause 9 | ✓ CA-6 | ✓ CC4.2 | ✓ Summary evidence | ✓ Summary evidence | ✓ Summary evidence
